<div id="review_110470621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110470621" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110470621?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110470621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9540206486337233245">I don't know what I expected when I picked this up for a group read, but it certainly wasn't what I got. This was like a blending of different things. Neil Gaiman's <i>Neverwhere</i> (which the author admitted to having inspired him) for its setting in an alternate London hidden from the regular one. Rowling's Harry Potter for the whole way the London children are discovering this world within our world, full of magic and wonder, as well as a double decker bus that has unusual properties. There was als</span>
  <span id="freeText9540206486337233245" style="display:none">I don't know what I expected when I picked this up for a group read, but it certainly wasn't what I got. This was like a blending of different things. Neil Gaiman's <i>Neverwhere</i> (which the author admitted to having inspired him) for its setting in an alternate London hidden from the regular one. Rowling's Harry Potter for the whole way the London children are discovering this world within our world, full of magic and wonder, as well as a double decker bus that has unusual properties. There was also a touch of the drab witty pessimism of Lemony Snicket's <i>Unfortunate Events</i> series. Throw in some Alice in Wonderland and you're close.<br /><br />But still, this may have elements of all these other stories, but it is its own as well. It's hard to talk about this without spoilers. <br /><br />I've seen it classified as "YA" or "middle reader" or "juvenile", but I didn't have any problem becoming interested. There is plenty of dry humor that adults will catch (and some that they might miss). <br /><br />One thing that Mi√©ville has going for him are the absurd creatures and characters and landmarks in UnLunDun. Some are funny, some are somewhat creepy, and some are positively brilliant. I could list some, but I don't want to take any of the delight away from discovering them by reading it.<br /><br />I'll close with: I want to see Tim Burton adapt this as a film!<br /><br />That is all.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9540206486337233245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21330169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21330169" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019174-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555890512p2/1019174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21330169?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/1019174-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345458445" href="/book/show/1861938.Un_Lun_Dun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019174-terence?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21330169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4806480582243872029">I wasn't sure whether or not to give this book a 3 or a 4 (if we had a more refined rating system, I'd give it a 3.7/3.8) because it started out a bit slow but as soon as Mieville focused on Deeba, the story picked up its pace and became much more interesting.<br/><br/>Short plot outline (which doesn't contain spoilers): Like many young-adult & adult fantasies, there's another version of London (and the world) that exists just "around the corner" or in between the stacks in a library that it's sometimes p</span>
  <span id="freeText4806480582243872029" style="display:none">I wasn't sure whether or not to give this book a 3 or a 4 (if we had a more refined rating system, I'd give it a 3.7/3.8) because it started out a bit slow but as soon as Mieville focused on Deeba, the story picked up its pace and became much more interesting.<br /><br />Short plot outline (which doesn't contain spoilers): Like many young-adult &amp; adult fantasies, there's another version of London (and the world) that exists just "around the corner" or in between the stacks in a library that it's sometimes possible to get to. In this case, it's the city of UnLondon, where the trash and the obsolete (like old-style double-decker buses) and lost laundry wind up. Everything there is alive, so Deeba winds up with a pet milk carton named Curdle.<br /><br />Zanna and Deeba are two young girls from London. Zanna is the Chosen One (the Shwazzy, corrupted French "choisir") prophesized to save UnLondon from the Smog (the sentient detritus of the pollution generated by our own world). Unfortunately, when they arrive, it turns out the prophecies were wrong and Zanna is dispatched (no, not killed, just "neutralized") rather easily by the Smog's minions. Fortunately, it appears that the Unbrellisimo, the ruler of the Unbrellas (no, that's not a mispelling, it's what broken umbrellas are called) has a plan to fight the Smog and everything looks like it will be all right so Zanna and Deeba return to London.<br /><br />In the process of being saved, Zanna forgets everything that occurred in UnLondon but Deeba remembers and stumbles upon the fact that the scientist Unstible, who created the formula by which the Unbrellas became effective weapons against the Smog, <i>died</i> in London so she knows something is wrong, and manages to return to UnLondon to find out what it is and save her friends.<br /><br />The rest of the novel is taken up with Deeba and her UnLondon friends' effort to save UnLondon.<br /><br />I wound up really enjoying this book. The moral of the book is that a person's fate is not set in stone, that people make their own fates. It also stresses the importance of friendship, and manages to get in lessons about recycling and preserving our environment without being preachy. It also displays Mieville's usual inventiveness.<br /><br />I'll be passing this along to my nieces, who may be a few years too young yet to appreciate it but will enjoy it eventually.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4806480582243872029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23705516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23705516" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23705516?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780230016279" href="/book/show/1031424.Un_Lun_Dun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=children-s-and-ya">children-s-and-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23705516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6061589645416464230">Un Lun Dun, by China Mi√©ville, is about the underside of London. The forgotten parts. So far, so very Neverwhere, I thought, at first. But actually, Un Lun Dun is a different kind of book. Cleverer, in that it twists fantasy clich√©s ("the UnChosen one" being the biggest example), quirkier (I didn't see a living milk carton called Curdle, or living ninja bins, binja, in Neverwhere!), and lighter. It's definitely aimed at younger people, and actually, I think China Mi√©ville does a good job of it. </span>
  <span id="freeText6061589645416464230" style="display:none">Un Lun Dun, by China Mi√©ville, is about the underside of London. The forgotten parts. So far, so very Neverwhere, I thought, at first. But actually, Un Lun Dun is a different kind of book. Cleverer, in that it twists fantasy clich√©s ("the UnChosen one" being the biggest example), quirkier (I didn't see a living milk carton called Curdle, or living ninja bins, binja, in Neverwhere!), and lighter. It's definitely aimed at younger people, and actually, I think China Mi√©ville does a good job of it. The pacing and description is much better than in Perdido Street Station, in my opinion, although the chapters are very short so sometimes it feels a bit choppy; possibly scene breaks would have been more appropriate than chapter breaks.<br /><br />I have to say, it is rather light on characterisation. Instead, it's more of a parade of quirky ideas -- Curdle, the binja, broken umbrellas having a life of their own... Normally, that'd be a problem for me. I'm very much the kind of person that gets attached to characters. Despite twisting the Chosen One archetype, the main characters ends up being rather the Chosen One type: smart, lucky, brave, etc, etc. <br /><br />It's not what you'd expect from China Mi√©ville, if you've read any of his other stuff. It's not the best example of his work, because I don't think it's representative. It's light, and very easy and quick to read. I think that makes it pretty fun.<br /><br />And in case you didn't notice, I <i>really</i> like Curdle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6061589645416464230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461615956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9114561592361293717">3.75 stars<br/><br/>My first introduction to Mi√©ville's writing was Railsea. I had an almost instant reaction to it (confusion, frustration, amazement) that only grew stronger as the story progressed (and changed into shock, awe and adoration, and finished with the literary equivalent of being hit on the head with a shovel). Un Lun Dun disappointed me for the supremely unfair (on my behalf) reason that it didn't draw much of a reaction from me.<br/><br/>I think that where YA and children's books are concerned, ther</span>
  <span id="freeText9114561592361293717" style="display:none">3.75 stars<br /><br />My first introduction to Mi√©ville's writing was Railsea. I had an almost instant reaction to it (confusion, frustration, amazement) that only grew stronger as the story progressed (and changed into shock, awe and adoration, and finished with the literary equivalent of being hit on the head with a shovel). Un Lun Dun disappointed me for the supremely unfair (on my behalf) reason that it didn't draw much of a reaction from me.<br /><br />I think that where YA and children's books are concerned, there are two essential kinds: those that cater only to the intended audience, and those that transcend these limits. Railsea is the later, Un Lun Dun the former and therein lies my disappointment.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Of course, there is a third category - those that are so terrible that NO ONE should like them, but that's totally irrelevant in this case, trust me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The story is vividly imagined, totally nuts, colourful, bright, simple to read and has strong characters and a good message. Perfect for a children's book. Mi√©ville cites Neil Gaiman as a huge influence, and this influence can be seen throughout - if Gaiman had written Neverwhere for a young audience, it would be something like Un Lun Dun. This is not to say that there is any blatant copying, or that the writing <i>style</i> is the same, only that the inspiration is plain to see. There is nothing wrong with this book. I just somehow wish there was a little more to it that would broaden its appeal to an older audience. This is no fault of the book's though, and who am I to criticise the author for simply catering to the intended audience? In fact, this book is now on my Christmas gift list for the younger siblings/cousins, who I know for a fact will absolutely adore this.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9114561592361293717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_116002548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116002548" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116002548?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345458445" href="/book/show/1861938.Un_Lun_Dun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116002548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12188929677027641427">(Maybe more sort of 2.5)<br/><br/>I was excited about the premise of this story. I like 'Wonderland' type stories, especially Gaiman's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere' title='Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neverwhere</a>, which Mieville does specifically mention as being an influence. But this story never really got above "alright" for me. <br/><br/>Part of the problem was that I never really clicked with or cared that much about the characters. I liked the role of Deeba at first - the friend who reluctantly gets dragged into an adventure - but I never really clicked with her as a person.</span>
  <span id="freeText12188929677027641427" style="display:none">(Maybe more sort of 2.5)<br /><br />I was excited about the premise of this story. I like 'Wonderland' type stories, especially Gaiman's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverwhere</a>, which Mieville does specifically mention as being an influence. But this story never really got above "alright" for me. <br /><br />Part of the problem was that I never really clicked with or cared that much about the characters. I liked the role of Deeba at first - the friend who reluctantly gets dragged into an adventure - but I never really clicked with her as a person. All the various secondary characters were interesting, but they never felt like fully fleshed out characters, and there were a lot of dialogue bits where the line could easily be interchanged from one person to another, because, really, they were just sort of there to fill out the ranks.<br /><br />The word play was interesting, but a bit groanworthy in places. The twists and turns were thoroughly predictable. I think, ultimately, especially in the first half of the book, it seems less like a cohesive whole world and more like a way for Mieville to drop every bit of quirky flotsam and jetsam he may have had floating around in his brain.<br /><br />It was sort of like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/768878.Abarat" title="Abarat by Clive Barker" rel="nofollow noopener">Abarat</a> this way, except that Barker's little vignettes were a bit darker and more original.<br /><br />It was an ok story, but it just didn't capture me.<br /><br />It hasn't entirely put me off trying more Mieville. I'm still interested in checking out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68494.Perdido_Street_Station" title="Perdido Street Station by China Mi√©ville" rel="nofollow noopener">Perdido Street Station</a> - but I'll definitely be getting it from the library if I do pick it up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12188929677027641427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_29212157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29212157" />
    <a title="Robert Beveridge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge"><img alt="Robert Beveridge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286387835p2/766524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29212157?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Beveridge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Beveridge" href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge">Robert Beveridge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=2008-goal-list">2008-goal-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=cuy-co-pub-lib">cuy-co-pub-lib</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=finished">finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=best-i-read-2008-edition">best-i-read-2008-edition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29212157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7458261150974953824">China Mieville, Un Lun Dun (Ballantine, 2007)<br/><br/>I have written many times (more than I can count, certainly) about the dangers of message fiction. Chief among them is that the author gets so wrapped up in the message that he forgets he's first and foremost supposed to tell a story. When I realized that Un Lun Dun, China Mieville's first childrens' book, was of the ‚Äúmessage fiction‚Äù stripe, I quailed in despair, thinking I might have encountered my first Mieville book (and I've read 'em all) I wasn'</span>
  <span id="freeText7458261150974953824" style="display:none">China Mieville, Un Lun Dun (Ballantine, 2007)<br /><br />I have written many times (more than I can count, certainly) about the dangers of message fiction. Chief among them is that the author gets so wrapped up in the message that he forgets he's first and foremost supposed to tell a story. When I realized that Un Lun Dun, China Mieville's first childrens' book, was of the ‚Äúmessage fiction‚Äù stripe, I quailed in despair, thinking I might have encountered my first Mieville book (and I've read 'em all) I wasn't going to like. I should have known better.<br /><br />Message-fiction writers, listen up: the vast majority of you have a lot to learn from China Mieville. This is how you tell a story. Not just a message story, but any story. (Which is the point, really.) Perfectly-created characters that are rich and deep, a strong plot in which to set them (with no end of surprises-- Mieville is also poking some fun at the traditional fantasy-novel setup here), a setting that manages to both be original and wear Mieville's debt to Clive Barker on its sleeve, and a message that, yes, still manages to poke its head through! Believe it or not, you can have all these things in one book! Don't believe me? Read this one.<br /><br />Un Lun Dun is the story of Zanna, the Shwazzy (I'd explain that, but catching the many puns in this book before Mieville reveals them is a lot of the fun-- and he still nailed me with Klinneract), and her friend Deeba. The two of them live in a block of apartments in London. Strange things start happening to them-- animals trying to communicate with them in sign language, odd-shaped clouds, being followed by a broken umbrella. Then Zanna goes into a basement, turns a wheel, and everything changes. I wish I could tell you more. I want to tell you more. But I don't want to spoil anything, anything at all, about this book. You deserve all the surprises, and all the delights, awaiting you when you read it for yourself. <br /><br />If you've encountered China Mieville before, you should know what to expect, except on a more YA level than you're used to. If you haven't experienced China Mieville before, hie thee to the library or the bookstore yesterday, if not before, and pick yourself up a copy of Perdido Street Station, one of the best books that's been published in the past decade in order to get acquainted. Though actually, I have to say, Un Lun Dun is the first book of his I've thought would also make an excellent entry point into Mieville's alternate universes (while most of his books are set in the invented world of Bas-Lag, his first novel King Rat and many of his shorter works are set in an alternate London somewhat similar to the one he uses here). One way or the other, though, I will not stop in my quest to get everyone I come into contact with to read China Mieville's stuff until, well, everyone has. And that includes you, so hop to it. **** ¬Ω<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7458261150974953824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_19993399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19993399" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858949-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19993399?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/858949-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19993399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6241912924748735186">A young girl in London is visited by strange people who seem to know her. They call her the <i>Schwazzy</i> and mysterious graffiti seems to imply that young Zannah is a mysterious savior-in-waiting. There's a mysterious world, unknown to most people, and only she can save them!<br/><br/>This is pretty much how the book begins. At this point, I found myself thinking, "How long will it be before people can read something like this without thinking of <i>Harry Potter</i>?" I mean, the whole displaced child-messiah thing </span>
  <span id="freeText6241912924748735186" style="display:none">A young girl in London is visited by strange people who seem to know her. They call her the <i>Schwazzy</i> and mysterious graffiti seems to imply that young Zannah is a mysterious savior-in-waiting. There's a mysterious world, unknown to most people, and only she can save them!<br /><br />This is pretty much how the book begins. At this point, I found myself thinking, "How long will it be before people can read something like this without thinking of <i>Harry Potter</i>?" I mean, the whole displaced child-messiah thing is fun, but Potter was a really big example of it and it'll take a long time before authors are able to overcome that. So, it was at this point that I settled in and got ready to read a nice boilerplate novel.<br /><br />Mister Mi√©ville, if you're reading this: I'm very, very sorry for not trusting you. It won't happen again.<br /><br />Mi√©ville has taken the child savior idea and pulled the rug out from under it in this book. While Zannah is the Chosen One of UnLondon, the one foretold about in the greatest prophecies of that abcity. It was said that she, with her friends, would defeat UnLondon's most horrible foe.... And if Mi√©ville had stuck with that, he still would have had a very entertaining book. With UnLondon, a kind of funhouse-mirror version of London, he's created a rich and vibrant city that can support tales of great complexity. That great city wants Zannah to save it.<br /><br />But right around a hundred pages in, Mi√©ville goes and switches protagonists on us. Just because a girl is the Chosen One doesn't mean that she has to end up being the one to save it. A good thwack on the head can make it so that the Funny Sidekick - Zannah's friend Deeba - is now the one who has to save UnLondon from The Smog.<br /><br />While Mi√©ville owes a great debt to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a> for his writing of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverwhere</a> - which he acknowledges in the end of the book - he's taken the concept of the Other London (to say nothing of other abcities such as Lost Angeles or Baghdidn't) and extended it. He's created a potentially vast other world, a network of cities that reflect our world in weird and wonderful ways. Deeba and her companions - embodied slang, a half-ghost boy and an animate milk carton named Curdle, to name just a few - embark on a quest to save a world from itself. It's a great story, full of adventure and twists which takes the expected standards of the genre and stands them on their head. For that alone, he should be praised. That, and for writing an awesome book....</span>
  <a data-text-id="6241912924748735186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_630008624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630008624" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8957684-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487520317p2/8957684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630008624?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/8957684-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345458445" href="/book/show/1861938.Un_Lun_Dun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8957684-daniel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8957684-daniel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8957684-daniel?shelf=simple-and-clean">simple-and-clean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8957684-daniel?shelf=8">8</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630008624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17006569016277437279"><b>China Mi√©ville</b><br/>Un Lun Dun<br/>Del Rey<br/>470 pages<br/>8.0 <br/><br/>In "Un Lun Dun"'s acknowledgment page, <a href='http://chinamieville.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mi√©ville</a> specifically thanks <a href='https://twitter.com/neilhimself' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neil Gaiman</a> for "generous encouragement and for his indispensable contributions to London phantasmagoria, especially "<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere' title='Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Neverwhere</a>". "Un Lun Dun"'s resemblance with "Neverwhere" is undeniable. Both take place in the hidden <a href='http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/CityOfAdventure' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Adventure</a> of London, with a fascinating worldbuilding and obscure creatures. I haven't read the whole "Neverwhere"--I first borrowed it from my friend back whe</span>
  <span id="freeText17006569016277437279" style="display:none"><b>China Mi√©ville</b><br />Un Lun Dun<br />Del Rey<br />470 pages<br />8.0 <br /><br />In "Un Lun Dun"'s acknowledgment page, <a href="http://chinamieville.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">Mi√©ville</a> specifically thanks <a href="https://twitter.com/neilhimself" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a> for "generous encouragement and for his indispensable contributions to London phantasmagoria, especially "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverwhere</a>". "Un Lun Dun"'s resemblance with "Neverwhere" is undeniable. Both take place in the hidden <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/CityOfAdventure" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Adventure</a> of London, with a fascinating worldbuilding and obscure creatures. I haven't read the whole "Neverwhere"--I first borrowed it from my friend back when I was still in seventh grade and my brain hadn't evolved fully so I couldn't grasp Gaiman's ingeniousness--but overall nuance of "Un Lun Dun" is pretty much similar. <br /><br />"Un Lun Dun" is an imaginative book that makes your part of brain that's in charge of imagination drudge extra hard. It churns your mind with splendid and smelly worldbuilding, with an interesting villain (a smog!), and magical creatures that people will never imagine before: carnivorous giraffes, dexterous bus, people who has birdcage as a head, the most scariest window. "Un Lun Dun" is a psychedelic steampunk--if that were ever a thing--and a perfect example that young adult book can be as bizarre as possible. <br /><br />It features a likable <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/DecoyProtagonist" rel="nofollow noopener">decoy protagonist</a> and great concept, but lack of binding that connects the whole story. The plot is typical RPG thing--a quest to save the world and collect some important items along the journey. But, Mi√©ville has spread a lot of red herring and Chekhov's Gun along the story, that I hope he will fire the gun at some time of the plot. But, no. He decides to keep the gun in safe position and doesn't fire it, and somehow it's disappointing because he has tons of ammo to awe me.<br /><br />But other than that, Un Lun Dun still remains as the most obscure books that I've ever read, and that's good. <br /><br />The review can be read <a href="http://bit.ly/21CVUfU" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

<div id="review_175942855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175942855" />
    <a title="J.P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5286233-j-p"><img alt="J.P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515332262p2/5286233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175942855?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.P." href="/user/show/5286233-j-p">J.P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5286233-j-p?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175942855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1580749287123615410">If there was an award given for most imagination used in a novel, China Mi√©ville would have more trophies than he would know what to do with.<br/>The man really outdoes himself in this one as he introduces a multitude of fascinating characters who are to say the least rather unusual. A man with a bird in a cage for a head, no-nonsense garbage cans wielding nunchucks appropriately called binjas, and the creepy black windows of Webminster Abbey, just to name a few.<br/>The comparison to <i> Alice in Wonderland</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1580749287123615410" style="display:none">If there was an award given for most imagination used in a novel, China Mi√©ville would have more trophies than he would know what to do with.<br />The man really outdoes himself in this one as he introduces a multitude of fascinating characters who are to say the least rather unusual. A man with a bird in a cage for a head, no-nonsense garbage cans wielding nunchucks appropriately called binjas, and the creepy black windows of Webminster Abbey, just to name a few.<br />The comparison to <i> Alice in Wonderland </i> is obvious but it would be an injustice to compare the two. The world of Un Lun Dun is uniquely Mi√©villian, typically dark and forbidding with many gosh I didn‚Äôt see that coming moments. The plot proceeds along a twisting path while avoiding the mundane. Every chapter seems to bring forth a new revelation. Alliances are forged as the backdrop changes yet again. What dangerous creature sporting an ugly mug will appear next?<br />The author also kicks to the curb all the stereotypical clich√©s so common in YA fiction. It‚Äôs the unexpected here folks. Like a talking book of knowledge written by clods. There are no easy solutions. Well, maybe except for the UnGun but even that has a different twist.<br />One teeny item about the plot might have been done differently. It relies a shade much on the ‚Äúis this person a good guy or a bad guy?‚Äù routine but overall it doesn‚Äôt matter. It‚Äôs like complaining the Mona Lisa has a speck of dust in a corner.<br />I‚Äôve rarely had so much fun reading a book written for a younger audience. If the author can make me root for an empty milk carton he can do anything. Recommended for everyone. If you‚Äôre a fan, for pity‚Äôs sake read this pronto! And if you aren‚Äôt you will be in short order. 5 stars all the way.<br /></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gvap/G4vArVRYVZHl+YAcasOgtjiPSDXUPV2N4tXbm5agGtjVfhvGgq8WvgEUVIsSZda7b6aqHhAcIGNqr42mg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FSE9U0ZnW65CQLEwvxwLKBheMD6Ab2gVX5iGSuKg9lHNV//MfbA2ARmdvY8sq1l1+sfoC9zI4LpPHXHww0mupQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6660889843259584014">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clich√©s of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist W</span>
  <span id="freeText6660889843259584014" style="display:none">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clich√©s of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist Workers Party. He has stood for the House of Commons for the Socialist Alliance, and published a book on Marxism and international law.<br /><br /><i>Excerpted from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_Mi%C3%A9ville" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a>.</i></span>

        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

</script>
